           <a href="/wiki/French_articles_and_determiners" title="French articles and determiners">
            Articles and determiners
           </a>
          </li>
          <li>

          </li>

            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:French_language&amp;action=edit">

      <p>
       <b>
        French
       </b>
       (
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         <i>
          le français
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">
         [lə fʁɑ̃sɛ]
        </a>
       </span>
       <small class="nowrap">
        (
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Fr-le_fran%C3%A7ais-fr-ouest.ogg" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/43/Fr-le_fran%C3%A7ais-fr-ouest.ogg" title="Fr-le français-fr-ouest.ogg">
           listen
          </a>
         </span>
        </span>
        )
       </small>
       or
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         <i>
          la langue française
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">
         [la lɑ̃ɡ fʁɑ̃sɛz]
        </a>
       </span>
       ) is a
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance language
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">
        Indo-European family
       </a>
       . It descended from the
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       , as did all Romance languages. French has evolved from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallo-Romance" title="Gallo-Romance">
        Gallo-Romance
       </a>
       , the spoken Latin in
       <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">
        Gaul
       </a>
       , and more specifically in Northern Gaul. Its closest relatives are the other
       <a href="/wiki/Langues_d%27o%C3%AFl" title="Langues d'oïl">
        langues d'oïl
       </a>
       —languages historically spoken in northern France and in southern
       <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">
        Belgium
       </a>
       , which French (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francien" title="Francien">
        Francien
       </a>
       ) has largely supplanted. French was also
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Substratum" title="Substratum">
        influenced
       </a>
       by native
       <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">
        Celtic languages
       </a>
       of Northern Roman Gaul like
       <a href="/wiki/Gallia_Belgica" title="Gallia Belgica">
        Gallia Belgica
       </a>
       and by the (
       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">
        Germanic
       </a>
       )
       <a href="/wiki/Frankish_language" title="Frankish language">
        Frankish language
       </a>
       of the post-Roman
       <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">
        Frankish
       </a>
       invaders. Today, owing to France's past overseas expansion, there are numerous
       <a href="/wiki/French-based_creole_languages" title="French-based creole languages">
        French-based creole languages
       </a>
       , most notably
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole_language" title="Haitian Creole language">
        Haitian Creole
       </a>
       . A French-speaking person or nation may be referred to as "
       <b>
        Francophone
       </b>
       " in both English and French.
      </p>
      <p>
       French is an
       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">
        official language
       </a>
       in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_where_French_is_an_official_language" title="List of countries where French is an official language">
        29 countries
       </a>
       across five different continents,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       most of which are members of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">
         Organisation internationale de la Francophonie
        </a>
       </i>
       (OIF), the community of 84 countries which share the official use or teaching of French. It is spoken as a first language (in descending order of the highest number) in
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       , the Canadian provinces of
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">
        Quebec
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">
        New Brunswick
       </a>
       , the regions of
       <a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">
        Wallonia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">
        Brussels
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">
        Belgium
       </a>
       , western
       <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
        Switzerland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">
        Monaco
       </a>
       , certain other
       <a href="/wiki/French_language_in_Canada#Francophones_across_Canada" title="French language in Canada">
        regions
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
        Canada
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">
        Louisiana
       </a>
       and the northern parts of
       <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">
        Maine
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">
        New Hampshire
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">
        Vermont
       </a>
       ), and by various communities elsewhere. In 2015, approximately 40% of the francophone population (including
       <a href="/wiki/Second_language" title="Second language">
        L2
       </a>
       and partial speakers) lived in Europe, 35% in sub-Saharan Africa, 15% in North Africa and the Middle East, 8% in the Americas, and 1% in Asia and Oceania.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OIF_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-OIF-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       French is the fourth most widely spoken mother tongue in the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nativeLanguages_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nativeLanguages-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Of Europeans who speak other languages natively, approximately one-fifth are able to speak French as a second language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       French is the second most taught foreign language in the EU.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       French is also the sixth most spoken language in the world, behind Mandarin Chinese, English, Hindi, Spanish, and Arabic, and is the second most studied language worldwide (with about 120 million current learners).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As a result of French and Belgian colonialism from the 16th century onward, French was introduced to new territories in the Americas, Africa and Asia. Most second-language speakers reside in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francophone_Africa" title="Francophone Africa">
        Francophone Africa
       </a>
       , in particular
       <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">
        Gabon
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">
        Algeria
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">
        Mauritius
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">
        Senegal
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">
        Ivory Coast
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2005_report_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-2005_report-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       French is estimated to have about 76 million native speakers,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethnologuefrench_1-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-ethnologuefrench-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Qu'est-ce_que_la_Francophonie_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Qu'est-ce_que_la_Francophonie-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and another 77 to 110 million secondary speakers to varying degrees of proficiency, mainly in Africa.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">
        Organisation internationale de la Francophonie
       </a>
       (OIF), approximately 274 million people worldwide are "able to speak the language", without specifying the criteria for this estimation or whom it encompasses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to a demographic projection led by the
       <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Laval" title="Université Laval">
        Université Laval
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Agence_universitaire_de_la_Francophonie" title="Agence universitaire de la Francophonie">
        Réseau Démographie de l'Agence universitaire de la francophonie
       </a>
       , total number of French speakers will reach approximately 500 million in 2025 and 650 million by 2050.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       OIF estimates 700 million by 2050, 80% of whom will be in Africa.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OIF_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-OIF-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       French has a long history as an international language of literature and scientific standards and is a primary or second language of many international organisations including the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty_Organization" title="North Atlantic Treaty Organization">
        North Atlantic Treaty Organization
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">
        World Trade Organization
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">
        International Olympic Committee
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">
        International Committee of the Red Cross
       </a>
       . In 2011,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_Businessweek" title="Bloomberg Businessweek">
         Bloomberg Businessweek
        </a>
       </i>
       ranked French the third most useful language for business, after
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Mandarin_Chinese" title="Standard Mandarin Chinese">
        Standard Mandarin Chinese
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lauerman2011_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lauerman2011-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

                   </span>

                    Subjunctive (Subjonctif)
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </li>
                 <li class="toclevel-5 tocsection-30">
                  <a href="#Imperative_(Imperatif)">
                   <span class="tocnumber">
                    7.2.1.1.3
                   </span>

                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </li>
                 <li class="toclevel-5 tocsection-31">
                  <a href="#Conditional_(Conditionnel)">

                    7.2.1.1.4
                   </span>

                    Conditional (Conditionnel)
                   </span>
                  </a>
                 </li>
                </ul>
               </li>
               <li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-32">
                <a href="#Non-Finite_moods">
                 <span class="tocnumber">
                  7.2.1.2
                 </span>
                 <span class="toctext">
                  Non-Finite moods
                 </span>
                </a>
                <ul>
                 <li class="toclevel-5 tocsection-33">
                  <a href="#Infinitive_(Infinitif)">

             </li>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_distribution">
        Geographic distribution
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geographical_distribution_of_French_speakers" title="Geographical distribution of French speakers">
        Geographical distribution of French speakers
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">
        Europe
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Knowledge_of_French_EU_map.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1242" data-file-width="1212" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Knowledge_of_French_EU_map.svg/220px-Knowledge_of_French_EU_map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Knowledge_of_French_EU_map.svg/330px-Knowledge_of_French_EU_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Knowledge_of_French_EU_map.svg/440px-Knowledge_of_French_EU_map.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Knowledge_of_French_EU_map.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Knowledge of French in the
         <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
          European Union
         </a>
         and candidate countries
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
          <a href="#cite_note-16">
           [16]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Spoken by 12% of the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       's population, French is the fourth most widely spoken mother tongue in the EU after German, English and Italian; it is also the third-most widely known language of the Union after English and German (33% of the EU population report knowing how to speak English, 22% of Europeans understand German, 20% French).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nativeLanguages_6-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-nativeLanguages-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Under the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_France" title="Constitution of France">
        Constitution of France
       </a>
       , French has been the official language of the Republic since 1992
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Benet-MartínezHong2014_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Benet-MartínezHong2014-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (although the
       <a href="/wiki/Ordinance_of_Villers-Cotter%C3%AAts" title="Ordinance of Villers-Cotterêts">
        ordinance of Villers-Cotterêts
       </a>
       made it mandatory for legal documents in 1539).
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       mandates the use of French in official government publications, public education except in specific cases (though these dispositions
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2016)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       are often ignored) and legal
       <a href="/wiki/Contract" title="Contract">
        contracts
       </a>
       ; advertisements must bear a translation of foreign words.
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">
        Belgium
       </a>
       , French is the official language of
       <a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">
        Wallonia
       </a>
       (excluding a part of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Cantons" title="East Cantons">
        East Cantons
       </a>
       , which are
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German-speaking
       </a>
       ) and one of the two official languages—along with
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">
        Dutch
       </a>
       —of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brussels-Capital_Region" title="Brussels-Capital Region">
        Brussels-Capital Region
       </a>
       , where it is spoken by the majority of the population often as their primary language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-philippevanparijs_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-philippevanparijs-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       French is one of the four official languages of
       <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
        Switzerland
       </a>
       (along with
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
        Italian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Romansh_language" title="Romansh language">
        Romansh
       </a>
       ) and is spoken in the western part of Switzerland called
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romandie" title="Romandie">
         Romandie
        </a>
       </i>
       , of which
       <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">
        Geneva
       </a>
       is the largest city. The language divisions in Switzerland do not coincide with political subdivisions, and some
       <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Switzerland" title="Cantons of Switzerland">
        cantons
       </a>
       have bilingual status: for example, cities such as
       <a href="/wiki/Biel/Bienne" title="Biel/Bienne">
        Biel/Bienne
       </a>
       and cantons such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canton_of_Valais" title="Canton of Valais">
        Valais
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Fribourg" title="Canton of Fribourg">
        Fribourg
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canton_of_Berne" title="Canton of Berne">
        Berne
       </a>
       . French is the native language of about 23% of the Swiss population, and is spoken by 50.4%
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       of the population.
      </p>
      <p>
       French is also an official language of
       <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">
        Monaco
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">
        Luxembourg
       </a>
       , as well as in the
       <a href="/wiki/Aosta_Valley" title="Aosta Valley">
        Aosta Valley
       </a>
       region of Italy, while French dialects remain spoken by minorities on the
       <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">
        Channel Islands
       </a>
       . It is also spoken in
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">
        Andorra
       </a>
       and is main communication language after
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/El_Pas_de_la_Casa" title="El Pas de la Casa">
        El Pas de la Casa
       </a>
       . The language is taught as the primary second language in the German
       <i>
        land
       </i>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Saarland" title="Saarland">
        Saarland
       </a>
       , with French being taught from pre-school and over 43% of citizens being able to speak French.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">
        Africa
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/African_French" title="African French">
        African French
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Francophone_Africa.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1230" data-file-width="1200" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Francophone_Africa.svg/220px-Francophone_Africa.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Francophone_Africa.svg/330px-Francophone_Africa.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Francophone_Africa.svg/440px-Francophone_Africa.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Francophone_Africa.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #006BA8; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Countries usually considered part of Francophone Africa.
          <br/>
          Their population was 410 million in 2017,
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2017_data_sheet_23-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-2017_data_sheet-23">
            [23]
           </a>
          </sup>
          and it is forecast to reach between 848 million
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
           <a href="#cite_note-24">
            [24]
           </a>
          </sup>
          and 867 million
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2017_data_sheet_23-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-2017_data_sheet-23">
            [23]
           </a>
          </sup>
          in 2050.
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00AAE2; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Countries sometimes considered as Francophone Africa
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #008080; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Countries that are not Francophone but are Members or Observers of the
          <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">
           OIF
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       A bulk of the world's French-speaking population lives in Africa. According to the 2007 report by the Organisation Internationale de la Francophonie, an estimated 115 million African people spread across 31 Francophone countries can speak French as either a
       <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">
        first
       </a>
       or a
       <a href="/wiki/Second_language" title="Second language">
        second language
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2005_report_10-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-2005_report-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This number does not include the people living in non-Francophone African countries who have learned French as a foreign language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2005_report_10-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2005_report-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Due to the rise of French in Africa, the total French-speaking population worldwide is expected to reach 700 million people in 2050.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       French is the fastest growing language on the continent (in terms of either official or foreign languages).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       French is mostly a second language in Africa, but it has become a first language in some urban areas, such as the region of
       <a href="/wiki/Abidjan" title="Abidjan">
        Abidjan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">
        Ivory Coast
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and in
       <a href="/wiki/Libreville" title="Libreville">
        Libreville
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">
        Gabon
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CEFAN_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CEFAN-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There is not a single
       <a href="/wiki/African_French" title="African French">
        African French
       </a>
       , but multiple forms that diverged through contact with various indigenous
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_languages" title="African languages">
        African languages
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">
        Sub-Saharan Africa
       </a>
       is the region where the French language is most likely to expand, because of the expansion of education and rapid population growth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is also where the language has evolved the most in recent years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some vernacular forms of French in Africa can be difficult to understand for French speakers from other countries,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but written forms of the language are very closely related to those of the rest of the French-speaking world.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Americas">
        Americas
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_North_America" title="Languages of North America">
        Languages of North America
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_South_America" title="Languages of South America">
        Languages of South America
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Caribbean" title="Languages of the Caribbean">
        Languages of the Caribbean
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arret.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="580" data-file-width="456" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Arret.jpg/170px-Arret.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Arret.jpg/255px-Arret.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Arret.jpg/340px-Arret.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arret.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Stop_sign" title="Stop sign">
          "arrêt" signs
         </a>
         (French for "stop") are used in
         <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
          Canada
         </a>
         while the English
         <i>
          stop,
         </i>
         which is also a valid French word, is used in France as well as other French-speaking countries and regions.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       French is the second most common language in
       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
        Canada
       </a>
       , after
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       , and both are official languages at the federal level. It is the first language of 9.5 million people or 29% and the second language for 2.07 million or 6% of the entire population of Canada.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Qu'est-ce_que_la_Francophonie_11-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Qu'est-ce_que_la_Francophonie-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       French is the sole official language in the province of
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">
        Quebec
       </a>
       , being the mother tongue for some 7 million people, or almost 80% (2006 Census) of the province. About 95% of the people of Quebec speak French as either their first or second language, and for some as their third language. Quebec is also home to the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">
        Montreal
       </a>
       , which is the world's 4th-largest French-speaking city, by number of first language speakers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">
        New Brunswick
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">
        Manitoba
       </a>
       are the only officially bilingual provinces, though full bilingualism is enacted only in New Brunswick, where about one third of the population is Francophone. French is also an official language of all of the territories (
       <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territories" title="Northwest Territories">
        Northwest Territories
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nunavut" title="Nunavut">
        Nunavut
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Yukon" title="Yukon">
        Yukon
       </a>
       ). Out of the three, Yukon has the most French speakers, comprising just under 4% of the population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Furthermore, while French is not an official language in
       <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">
        Ontario
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/French_Language_Services_Act" title="French Language Services Act">
        French Language Services Act
       </a>
       ensures that provincial services are to be available in the language. The Act applies to areas of the province where there are significant Francophone communities, namely
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Ontario" title="Eastern Ontario">
        Eastern Ontario
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ontario" title="Northern Ontario">
        Northern Ontario
       </a>
       . Elsewhere, sizable French-speaking minorities are found in southern Manitoba,
       <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">
        Nova Scotia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">
        Prince Edward Island
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Port_au_Port_Peninsula" title="Port au Port Peninsula">
        Port au Port Peninsula
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">
        Newfoundland and Labrador
       </a>
       , where the unique
       <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_French" title="Newfoundland French">
        Newfoundland French
       </a>
       dialect was historically spoken. Smaller pockets of French speakers exist in all other provinces. The city of Ottawa, the Canadian capital, is also effectively bilingual, as it is on the other side of a river from Quebec, opposite the major city of Gatineau, and is required to offer governmental services in French as well as English.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:French_in_the_United_States.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1222" data-file-width="1064" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/French_in_the_United_States.png/220px-French_in_the_United_States.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/French_in_the_United_States.png/330px-French_in_the_United_States.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/French_in_the_United_States.png/440px-French_in_the_United_States.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:French_in_the_United_States.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         French language spread in the United States. Counties marked in lighter pink are those where 6–12% of the population speaks French at home; medium pink, 12–18%; darker pink, over 18%.
         <a href="/wiki/French-based_creole_languages" title="French-based creole languages">
          French-based creole languages
         </a>
         are not included.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to the U.S. Census Bureau (2011), French is the fourth
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       most-spoken language in the United States after
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">
        Chinese
       </a>
       , when all forms of French are considered together and all dialects of Chinese are similarly combined. French remains the second most-spoken language in the states of
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">
        Louisiana
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">
        Maine
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">
        Vermont
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">
        New Hampshire
       </a>
       . Louisiana is home to many distinct dialects, collectively known as
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_French" title="Louisiana French">
        Louisiana French
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Cajun_French" title="Cajun French">
        Cajun French
       </a>
       has the largest number of speakers, mostly living in
       <a href="/wiki/Acadiana" title="Acadiana">
        Acadiana
       </a>
       . According to the 2000 United States Census, there are over 194,000 people in Louisiana who speak French at home, the most of any state if
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louisiana_Creole_French" title="Louisiana Creole French">
        Creole French
       </a>
       is excluded.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factfinder.census.gov_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-factfinder.census.gov-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/New_England_French" title="New England French">
        New England French
       </a>
       , essentially a variant of
       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_French" title="Canadian French">
        Canadian French
       </a>
       , is spoken in parts of
       <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">
        New England
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Missouri_French" title="Missouri French">
        Missouri French
       </a>
       was historically spoken in
       <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">
        Missouri
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">
        Illinois
       </a>
       (formerly known as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_Louisiana" title="Upper Louisiana">
        Upper Louisiana
       </a>
       ), but is nearly extinct today.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       French is one of Haiti's two official languages. It is the principal language of writing, school instruction, and administrative use. It is spoken by all educated Haitians and is used in the business sector. It is also used for ceremonial events such as weddings, graduations and church masses. About 70–80% of the country's population have Haitian Creole as their first language; the rest speak French as a first language. The second official language is the recently standardized
       <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole" title="Haitian Creole">
        Haitian Creole
       </a>
       , which virtually the entire population of Haiti speaks. Haitian Creole is one of the
       <a href="/wiki/French-based_creole_languages" title="French-based creole languages">
        French-based creole languages
       </a>
       , drawing the large majority of its vocabulary from French, with influences from West African languages, as well as several European languages. Haitian Creole is closely related to Louisiana Creole and the creole from the
       <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">
        Lesser Antilles
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       French is the official language of both
       <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">
        French Guiana
       </a>
       on the South American continent,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and of
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Pierre_and_Miquelon" title="Saint Pierre and Miquelon">
        Saint Pierre and Miquelon
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       an archipelago off the coast of Newfoundland in North America.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:France_colonial_Empire10.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1357" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/France_colonial_Empire10.png/220px-France_colonial_Empire10.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/France_colonial_Empire10.png/330px-France_colonial_Empire10.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/France_colonial_Empire10.png/440px-France_colonial_Empire10.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:France_colonial_Empire10.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Areas of French Colonization
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">
        Asia
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast_Asia">
        Southeast Asia
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/French_language_in_Vietnam" title="French language in Vietnam">
        French language in Vietnam
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/French_language_in_Laos" title="French language in Laos">
        French language in Laos
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/French_language_in_Cambodia" title="French language in Cambodia">
        French language in Cambodia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       French was the official language of the colony of
       <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">
        French Indochina
       </a>
       , comprising modern-day
       <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">
        Vietnam
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">
        Laos
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">
        Cambodia
       </a>
       . It continues to be an administrative language in Laos and Cambodia, although its influence has waned in recent years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In colonial Vietnam, the elites primarily spoke French, while many servants who worked in French households spoke a French pidgin known as "
       <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A2y_B%E1%BB%93i_Pidgin_French" title="Tây Bồi Pidgin French">
        Tây Bồi
       </a>
       " (now extinct). After French rule ended,
       <a href="/wiki/South_Vietnam" title="South Vietnam">
        South Vietnam
       </a>
       continued to use French in administration, education, and trade.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since the
       <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Saigon" title="Fall of Saigon">
        Fall of Saigon
       </a>
       and the opening of a unified Vietnam's economy, French has gradually been effectively displaced as the main foreign language of choice by English. French nevertheless maintains its colonial legacy by being spoken as a second language by the elderly and elite populations and is presently being revived in higher education and continues to be a diplomatic language in Vietnam. All three countries are official members of the OIF.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_East">
        Middle East
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Lebanon">
        Lebanon
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/French_language_in_Lebanon" title="French language in Lebanon">
        French language in Lebanon
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bienvenue_a_Rechmaya.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="564" data-file-width="843" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Bienvenue_a_Rechmaya.jpg/150px-Bienvenue_a_Rechmaya.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Bienvenue_a_Rechmaya.jpg/225px-Bienvenue_a_Rechmaya.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Bienvenue_a_Rechmaya.jpg/300px-Bienvenue_a_Rechmaya.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bienvenue_a_Rechmaya.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Town sign in
         <a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">
          Standard Arabic
         </a>
         and French at the entrance of
         <a href="/wiki/Rechmaya" title="Rechmaya">
          Rechmaya
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">
          Lebanon
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       A former French colony,
       <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">
        Lebanon
       </a>
       designates
       <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">
        Arabic
       </a>
       as the sole official language, while a special law regulates cases when French can be publicly used. Article 11 of Lebanon's Constitution states that "Arabic is the official national language. A law determines the cases in which the French language is to be used".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-article_11_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-article_11-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/French_language_in_Lebanon" title="French language in Lebanon">
        French language in Lebanon
       </a>
       is widely used as a second language by the
       <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">
        Lebanese people
       </a>
       , and is taught in many schools as a secondary language along with Arabic and English. The language is also used on
       <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_pound" title="Lebanese pound">
        Lebanese pound
       </a>
       bank notes, on road signs, on Lebanese
       <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_registration_plates_of_Lebanon" title="Vehicle registration plates of Lebanon">
        license plates
       </a>
       , and on official buildings (alongside Arabic).
      </p>
      <p>
       Today, French and English are secondary languages of
       <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">
        Lebanon
       </a>
       , with about 40% of the population being
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francophone" title="Francophone">
        Francophone
       </a>
       and 40% Anglophone.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOIF2014217_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOIF2014217-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The use of English is growing in the business and media environment. Out of about 900,000 students, about 500,000 are enrolled in Francophone schools, public or private, in which the teaching of mathematics and scientific subjects is provided in French.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOIF2014218_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOIF2014218-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Actual usage of French varies depending on the region and social status. One third of high school students educated in French go on to pursue higher education in English-speaking institutions. English is the language of business and communication, with French being an element of social distinction, chosen for its emotional value.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOIF2014358_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOIF2014358-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On social media, French was used on Facebook by just 10% of Lebanese in 2014, far behind English (78%).
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Syria">
        Syria
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Similarly to Lebanon,
       <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
        Syria
       </a>
       was also a French League of Nations-mandate area until 1943, but today the French language is largely limited to some members of the elite and middle classes.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">
        Israel
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       A significant French-speaking community is also present in
       <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
        Israel
       </a>
       , primarily among the communities of
       <a href="/wiki/French_Jews_in_Israel" title="French Jews in Israel">
        French Jews in Israel
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_Jews_in_Israel" title="Moroccan Jews in Israel">
        Moroccan Jews in Israel
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lebanese_Jews" title="Lebanese Jews">
        Lebanese Jews
       </a>
       . Many secondary schools offer French as a foreign language.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="United_Arab_Emirates_and_Qatar">
        United Arab Emirates and Qatar
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">
        UAE
       </a>
       has the status in the
       <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">
        Organisation internationale de la Francophonie
       </a>
       as an observer state, and
       <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">
        Qatar
       </a>
       has the status in the organization as an associate state. However, in both countries French is not spoken by almost any of the general population or migrant workers, but spoken by a small minority of those who invest in Francophone countries or have other financial or family ties. Their entrance as observer and associate states respectively into the organisation was aided a good deal by their investments into the Organisation and France itself.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A country's status as an observer state in the
       <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">
        Organisation internationale de la Francophonie
       </a>
       gives the country the right to send representatives to organization meetings and make formal requests to the organization but they do not have voting rights within the OIF.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A country's status as an associate state also does not give a country voting abilities but associate states can discuss and review organization matters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania_and_Australasia">
        Oceania and Australasia
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CFP_500_recto.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="254" data-file-width="462" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/CFP_500_recto.jpg/170px-CFP_500_recto.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/CFP_500_recto.jpg/255px-CFP_500_recto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/CFP_500_recto.jpg/340px-CFP_500_recto.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CFP_500_recto.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A 500-
         <a href="/wiki/CFP_franc" title="CFP franc">
          CFP franc
         </a>
         (€4.20; US$4.90) banknote, used in
         <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">
          French Polynesia
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">
          New Caledonia
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Wallis_and_Futuna" title="Wallis and Futuna">
          Wallis and Futuna
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       French is an official language of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Island" title="Pacific Island">
        Pacific Island
       </a>
       nation of
       <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">
        Vanuatu
       </a>
       where 45% of the population can speak French.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the French special collectivity of
       <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">
        New Caledonia
       </a>
       , 97% of the population can speak, read and write French, whereas only 1% have no knowledge of French.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">
        French Polynesia
       </a>
       , 95% of the population can speak, read and write French, whereas only 1.5% have no knowledge of French.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the French collectivity of
       <a href="/wiki/Wallis_and_Futuna" title="Wallis and Futuna">
        Wallis and Futuna
       </a>
       , 78% of the population can speak, read and write French, whereas 17% have no knowledge of French.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects">
        Dialects
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:

       </a>
      </div>

          Dialects of the French language in the world
