        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h6>
       <span id="Past_participle_.28Participe_pass.C3.A9.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Past_participle_(Participe_passé)">
        Past participle (Participe passé)
       </span>
      </h6>
      <p>
       The past participle is found in the past.
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Participe Passé
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         aimé
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Voice">
        Voice
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       French uses both the
       <a href="/wiki/Active_voice" title="Active voice">
        active voice
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Passive_voice" title="Passive voice">
        passive voice
       </a>
       . The active voice is unmarked while the passive voice is formed by using a form of verb
       <i>
        être
       </i>
       ("to be") and the past participle.
      </p>
      <p>
       Example of the active voice:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        "Elle aime le chien."
        <i>
         She loves the dog.
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        "Mark a conduit la voiture."
        <i>
         Mark drove the car.
        </i>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Example of the passive voice:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        "Le chien est aimé par elle."
        <i>
         The dog is loved by her.
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        "La voiture était conduite par Mark."
        <i>
         The car was driven by Mark.
        </i>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Syntax">
        Syntax
       </span>
      </h4>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Word_order">
        Word order
       </span>
      </h5>
      <p>
       French declarative word order is
       <a href="/wiki/Subject%E2%80%93verb%E2%80%93object" title="Subject–verb–object">
        subject–verb–object
       </a>
       although a pronoun object precedes the verb. Some types of sentences allow for or require different word orders, in particular
       <a href="/wiki/Inversion_(linguistics)" title="Inversion (linguistics)">
        inversion
       </a>
       of the subject and verb like "Parlez-vous français?" when asking a question rather than just "Vous parlez français ?" Both questions mean the same thing; however, a rising inflection is always used on both of them whenever asking a question, especially on the second one. Specifically, the first translates into "Do you speak French?" while the second one is literally just "You speak French?" To avoid inversion while asking a question, 'Est-ce que' (literally 'is it that') may be placed in the beginning of the sentence. "Parlez-vous français ?" may become "Est-ce que vous parlez français ?" French also uses
       <a href="/wiki/Verb%E2%80%93object%E2%80%93subject" title="Verb–object–subject">
        verb–object–subject (VOS)
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Object%E2%80%93subject%E2%80%93verb" title="Object–subject–verb">
        object–subject–verb (OSV)
       </a>
       word order. OSV word order is not used often and VOS is reserved for formal writings.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_59-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-auto-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">
        Vocabulary
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The majority of French words derive from
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       or were constructed from
       <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
        Latin
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">
        Greek
       </a>
       roots. In many cases a single etymological root appears in French in a "popular" or native form, inherited from Vulgar Latin, and a learned form, borrowed later from
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_Latin" title="Classical Latin">
        Classical Latin
       </a>
       . The following pairs consist of a native noun and a learned adjective:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        brother:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fr%C3%A8re" title="wikt:frère">
          frère
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fraternel" title="wikt:fraternel">
          fraternel
         </a>
        </i>
        from Latin
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/frater" title="wikt:frater">
          frater
         </a>
         /
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fraternalis" title="wikt:fraternalis">
          fraternalis
         </a>
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        finger:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/doigt" title="wikt:doigt">
          doigt
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/digital" title="wikt:digital">
          digital
         </a>
        </i>
        from Latin
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/digitus" title="wikt:digitus">
          digitus
         </a>
         /
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/digitalis" title="wikt:digitalis">
          digitalis
         </a>
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        faith:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/foi" title="wikt:foi">
          foi
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fid%C3%A8le" title="wikt:fidèle">
          fidèle
         </a>
        </i>
        from Latin
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fides" title="wikt:fides">
          fides
         </a>
         /
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fidelis" title="wikt:fidelis">
          fidelis
         </a>
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        eye:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%C5%93il" title="wikt:œil">
          œil
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/oculaire" title="wikt:oculaire">
          oculaire
         </a>
        </i>
        from Latin
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/oculus" title="wikt:oculus">
          oculus
         </a>
         /
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ocularis" title="wikt:ocularis">
          ocularis
         </a>
        </i>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       However, a historical tendency to gallicise Latin roots can be identified, whereas English conversely leans towards a more direct incorporation of the Latin:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/rayonnement" title="wikt:rayonnement">
          rayonnement
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         radiation
        </i>
        from Latin
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/radiatio" title="wikt:radiatio">
          radiatio
         </a>
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%C3%A9teindre" title="wikt:éteindre">
          éteindre
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         extinguish
        </i>
        from Latin
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/exstinguo#Latin" title="wikt:exstinguo">
          exstinguere
         </a>
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/noyau" title="wikt:noyau">
          noyau
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         nucleus
        </i>
        from Latin
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/nucleus#Latin" title="wikt:nucleus">
          nucleus
         </a>
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ensoleillement" title="wikt:ensoleillement">
          ensoleillement
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         insolation
        </i>
        from Latin
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/insolatio" title="wikt:insolatio">
          insolatio
         </a>
        </i>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       There are also noun-noun and adjective-adjective pairs:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        thing/cause:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/chose" title="wikt:chose">
          chose
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cause" title="wikt:cause">
          cause
         </a>
        </i>
        from Latin
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/causa" title="wikt:causa">
          causa
         </a>
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        cold:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/froid" title="wikt:froid">
          froid
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/frigide" title="wikt:frigide">
          frigide
         </a>
        </i>
        from Latin
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/frigidum" title="wikt:frigidum">
          frigidum
         </a>
        </i>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       It can be difficult to identify the Latin source of native French words, because in the evolution from
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       , unstressed syllables were severely reduced and the remaining vowels and consonants underwent significant modifications.
      </p>
      <p>
       More recently the linguistic policy of the French language academies of France and Quebec has been to provide French equivalents to (mainly English) imported words, either by using existing vocabulary, extending its meaning or deriving a new word according to French morphological rules. The result is often two (or more) co-existing terms for describing the same phenomenon.
      </p>

        </i>
       </li>

        </i>

      <p>
       It is estimated that 12% (4,200) of common French words found in a typical
       <a href="/wiki/Dictionary" title="Dictionary">
        dictionary
       </a>
       such as the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Petit_Larousse" title="Petit Larousse">
         Petit Larousse
        </a>
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Micro-Robert Plus
       </i>
       (35,000 words) are of foreign origin (where
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">
        Greek
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">
        Latin
       </a>
       learned words are not seen as foreign). About 25% (1,054) of these foreign words come from
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       and are fairly recent borrowings. The others are some 707 words from
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
        Italian
       </a>
       , 550 from ancient
       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">
        Germanic languages
       </a>
       , 481 from other
       <a href="/wiki/Gallo-Romance_languages" title="Gallo-Romance languages">
        Gallo-Romance languages
       </a>
       , 215 from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Arabic
       </a>
       , 164 from
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German
       </a>
       , 160 from
       <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">
        Celtic languages
       </a>
       , 159 from
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       , 153 from
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">
        Dutch
       </a>
       , 112 from
       <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">
        Persian
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sanskrit_language" title="Sanskrit language">
        Sanskrit
       </a>
       , 101 from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_languages" title="Native American languages">
        Native American languages
       </a>
       , 89 from other
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_languages" title="Asian languages">
        Asian languages
       </a>
       , 56 from other
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Asiatic_languages" title="Afro-Asiatic languages">
        Afro-Asiatic languages
       </a>
       , 55 from
       <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">
        Slavic languages
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_languages" title="Baltic languages">
        Baltic languages
       </a>
       , 10 from
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">
        Basque
       </a>
       and 144 (about 3%) from other languages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_85-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-auto1-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       One study analyzing the degree of differentiation of Romance languages in comparison to Latin estimated that among the languages analyzed French has the greatest distance from Latin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Lexical_similarity" title="Lexical similarity">
        Lexical similarity
       </a>
       is 89% with Italian, 80% with Sardinian, 78% with Rhaeto-Romance, and 75% with Romanian, Spanish and Portuguese.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethnologue.com_87-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ethnologue.com-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MED_88-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-MED-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethnologue.com_87-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ethnologue.com-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Numerals">
        Numerals
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The French counting system is partially
       <a href="/wiki/Vigesimal" title="Vigesimal">
        vigesimal
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/20_(number)" title="20 (number)">
        twenty
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         vingt
        </span>
       </i>
       ) is used as a base number in the names of numbers from 80 to 99. The French word for
       <i>
        80
       </i>
       is
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         quatre-vingts
        </span>
       </i>
       , literally "four twenties", and the word for
       <i>
        75
       </i>
       is
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         soixante-quinze
        </span>
       </i>
       , literally "sixty-fifteen". This reform arose after the
       <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">
        French Revolution
       </a>
       to unify the different counting systems (mostly vigesimal near the coast, because of Celtic (via
       <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">
        Breton
       </a>
       ) and Viking influences). This system is comparable to the archaic English use of
       <i>
        score
       </i>
       , as in "fourscore and seven" (87), or "threescore and ten" (70).
      </p>
      <p>
       In Old French (during the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
       ), all numbers from 30 to 99 could be said in either base 10 or base 20, e.g.
       <i>
        vint et doze
       </i>
       (twenty and twelve) for 32,
       <i>
        dous vinz et diz
       </i>
       (two twenties and ten) for 50,
       <i>
        uitante
       </i>
       for 80, or
       <i>
        nonante
       </i>
       for 90.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Belgian_French" title="Belgian French">
        Belgian French
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Swiss_French" title="Swiss French">
        Swiss French
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Aostan_French" title="Aostan French">
        Aostan French
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jean-Pierre_Martin_1984_90-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Jean-Pierre_Martin_1984-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the French used in the
       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">
        Democratic Republic of the Congo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">
        Rwanda
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">
        Burundi
       </a>
       are different in this respect. In the French spoken in these places, 70 and 90 are
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         septante
        </span>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         nonante
        </span>
       </i>
       . In Switzerland, depending on the local dialect, 80 can be
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         quatre-vingts
        </span>
       </i>
       (Geneva, Neuchâtel, Jura) or
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         huitante
        </span>
       </i>
       (Vaud, Valais, Fribourg).
       <i>
        Octante
       </i>
       had been used in
       <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
        Switzerland
       </a>
       in the past, but is now considered archaic,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while in the
       <a href="/wiki/Aosta_Valley" title="Aosta Valley">
        Aosta Valley
       </a>
       80 is
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         huitante
        </span>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jean-Pierre_Martin_1984_90-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Jean-Pierre_Martin_1984-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In Belgium and in its former African colonies, however,
       <i>
        quatre-vingts
       </i>
       is universally used.
      </p>
      <p>
       French, like most European languages, uses a space to separate thousands
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       where English uses a comma or (more recently) a space. The comma is used in French numbers as a decimal point: 2,5 =
       <i>
        deux virgule cinq
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Units">
        Units
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Cardinal numbers in French, from 0 to 20, are as follows:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Zero:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/z%C3%A9ro" title="wikt:zéro">
          zéro
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ze.ʁo/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        One:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/un" title="wikt:un">
          un
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/une" title="wikt:une">
          une
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /œ̃/
        </span>
        (m) ~
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /yn/
        </span>
        (f)
       </li>
       <li>
        Two:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/deux" title="wikt:deux">
          deux
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /dø/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Three:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/trois" title="wikt:trois">
          trois
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /tʁwɑ/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Four:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/quatre" title="wikt:quatre">
          quatre
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /katʁ/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Five:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cinq" title="wikt:cinq">
          cinq
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /sɛ̃k/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Six:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/six" title="wikt:six">

         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /sis/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Seven:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/sept" title="wikt:sept">

         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /sɛt/
        </span>

       <li>

         /ɥit/

         /nœf/
        </span>

       <li>

        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/dix" title="wikt:dix">

         /dis/
        </span>

       <li>

        </span>

        Seventeen:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/dix-sept" title="wikt:dix-sept">

        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /dissɛt/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Eighteen:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/dix-huit" title="wikt:dix-huit">

        </span>

       <li>

         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/vingt" title="wikt:vingt">
          vingt
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /vɛ̃/
        </span>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       After
       <i>
        Twenty
       </i>
       , numbers use base ten logic (
       <i>
        vingt et un
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        vingt-deux
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        vingt-trois
       </i>
       ...)
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tens">
        Tens
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Cardinal numbers in French, by tens from 10 to 100, are as follows:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Ten:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/dix" title="wikt:dix">
          dix
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /dis/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Twenty:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/vingt" title="wikt:vingt">
          vingt
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /vɛ̃/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Thirty:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/trente" title="wikt:trente">
          trente
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /tʁɑ̃t/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Forty:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/quarante" title="wikt:quarante">
          quarante
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ka.ʁɑ̃t/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Fifty:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cinquante" title="wikt:cinquante">
          cinquante
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /sɛ̃.kɑ̃t/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Sixty:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/soixante" title="wikt:soixante">
          soixante
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /swa.sɑ̃t/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Seventy:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/soixante-dix" title="wikt:soixante-dix">
          soixante-dix
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /swa.sɑ̃t.dis/
        </span>
        or
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/septante" title="wikt:septante">

         </a>

        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
         <a href="#cite_note-95">
          [b]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /sɛp.tɑ̃t/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Eighty:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/quatre-vingts" title="wikt:quatre-vingts">
          quatre-vingts
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ka.tʁɘ.vɛ̃/
        </span>
        ,
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/huitante" title="wikt:huitante">

         <a href="#cite_note-96">
          [c]
         </a>

        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ɥi.tɑ̃t/

        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/octante" title="wikt:octante">

        Ninety:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/quatre-vingt-dix" title="wikt:quatre-vingt-dix">

         /nɔ.nɑ̃t/

        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cent" title="wikt:cent">

        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /sɑ̃(t)/
        </span>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       After
       <i>
        One hundred
       </i>
       , numbers use base ten logic (
       <i>
        cent dix
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        cent vingt
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        cent trente
       </i>
       ...)
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hundreds">
        Hundreds
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Cardinal numbers in French, by hundreds from 100 to 2000, are as follows:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        One hundred:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cent" title="wikt:cent">
          cent
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /sɑ̃(t)/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Two hundred:
        <i>
         deux cents
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Three hundred:
        <i>
         trois cents
        </i>
        , (Archaism:
        <i>
         quinze-vingts
        </i>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        Four hundred:
        <i>
         quatre cents
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Five hundred:
        <i>
         cinq cents
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Six hundred:
        <i>
         six cents
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Seven hundred:
        <i>
         sept cents
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Eight hundred:
        <i>
         huit cents
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Nine hundred:
        <i>
         neuf cents
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        One thousand:
        <i>
         mille
        </i>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
         <a href="#cite_note-100">
          [f]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        One thousand one hundred:
        <i>
         onze cents
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         mille cent
        </i>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thousandByHundreds_103-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-thousandByHundreds-103">
          [g]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        One thousand two hundred:
        <i>
         douze cents
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         mille deux cents
        </i>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thousandByHundreds_103-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-thousandByHundreds-103">
          [g]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        One thousand three hundred:
        <i>
         treize cents
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         mille trois cents
        </i>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thousandByHundreds_103-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-thousandByHundreds-103">
          [g]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        One thousand four hundred:
        <i>
         quatorze cents
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         mille quatre cents
        </i>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thousandByHundreds_103-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-thousandByHundreds-103">
          [g]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        One thousand five hundred:
        <i>
         quinze cents
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         mille cinq cents
        </i>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thousandByHundreds_103-4">
         <a href="#cite_note-thousandByHundreds-103">
          [g]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        One thousand six hundred:
        <i>
         seize cents
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         mille six cents
        </i>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thousandByHundreds_103-5">
         <a href="#cite_note-thousandByHundreds-103">
          [g]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        One thousand seven hundred:
        <i>
         dix-sept cents
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         mille sept cents
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        One thousand eight hundred:
        <i>
         dix-huit cents
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         mille huit cents
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        One thousand nine hundred:
        <i>
         dix-neuf cents
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         mille neuf cents
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Two thousand:
        <i>
         deux mille
        </i>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       After
       <i>
        deux mille
       </i>
       (2000), only the second option is used (
       <i>
        deux mille cent
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        deux mille deux cents
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        deux mille trois cents
       </i>
       ...)
      </p>
      <p>
       The words
       <i>
        vingt
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        cent
       </i>
       take the plural
       <b>
        -s
       </b>
       only when they are the last word of the number:
       <i>
        quatre-vingts
       </i>
       (eighty) and
       <i>
        quatre-vingt-un
       </i>
       (eighty-one),
       <i>
        cinq cents
       </i>
       (five hundred) and
       <i>
        cinq cent trente
       </i>
       (five hundred and thirty). When a number using
       <i>
        vingt
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        cent
       </i>
       is used as an ordinal numeral adjective, the words
       <i>
        vingt
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        cent
       </i>
       stay unchanged.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="Scales.5Bh.5D">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Scales[h]">
        Scales
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
         <a href="#cite_note-105">
          [h]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Cardinal numbers in French, by exponentiation points, from 10
       <sup>
        0
       </sup>
       to 10
       <sup>
        20
       </sup>
       , are as follows:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        One:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/un" title="wikt:un">
          un
         </a>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/une" title="wikt:une">
          une
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /œ̃/
        </span>
        (m) ~
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /yn/
        </span>
        (f)
       </li>
       <li>
        Ten:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/dix" title="wikt:dix">
          dix
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /dis/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        One hundred:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cent" title="wikt:cent">
          cent
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /sɑ̃(t)/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        One thousand:
        <i>
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/mille" title="wikt:mille">
          mille
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /mil/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Ten thousand:
        <i>
         dix mille
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Hundred thousand:
        <i>
         cent mille
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        One million:
        <i>
         un
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/million" title="wikt:million">
          million
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /mi.ljɔ̃/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Ten million:
        <i>
         dix millions
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Hundred million:
        <i>
         cent millions
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        One billion:
        <i>
         un
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/milliard" title="wikt:milliard">
          milliard
         </a>
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Ten billion:
        <i>
         dix milliards
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Hundred billion:
        <i>
         cent milliards
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        One trillion:
        <i>
         un
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/billion" title="wikt:billion">
          billion
         </a>
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /bi.ljɔ̃/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Ten trillion:
        <i>
         dix billions
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Hundred trillion:
        <i>
         cent billions
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        One quadrillion:
        <i>
         un
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/billiard" title="wikt:billiard">
          billiard
         </a>
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Ten quadrillion:
        <i>
         dix billiards
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Hundred quadrillion:
        <i>
         cent billiards
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        One quintillion:
        <i>
         un
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/trillion" title="wikt:trillion">
          trillion
         </a>
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Ten quintillion:
        <i>
         dix trillions
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        Hundred quintillion:
        <i>
         cent trillions
        </i>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       <b>
        Notes
       </b>
      </p>
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references">
         <li id="cite_note-94">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-94">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           It has been suggested that
           <i>
            Nine
           </i>
           and
           <i>
            New
           </i>
           homophonographs are related and that it would be an unusual preservation of the
           <a href="/wiki/Octal" title="Octal">
            octal
           </a>
           number system speculated to be formerly used in
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European" title="Proto-Indo-European">
            proto-Indo-European
           </a>
           language, though the evidence supporting this is slim.
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
            <a href="#cite_note-93">
             [93]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-95">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-95">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <i>
            Septante
           </i>
           is used in Belgium and in Switzerland. Its use is dated in Eastern France and archaic elsewhere in France.
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-96">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-96">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <i>
            Huitante
           </i>
           is used in Vaud, Valais, Fribourg, archaic in France.
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-97">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-97">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <i>
            Octante
           </i>
           is used, but dated, in Romandie and in Southern France. Its use is archaic in other parts of France.
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-98">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-98">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <i>
            Nonante
           </i>
           is used in Belgium, Switzerland and, dated, in Eastern France, archaic in other parts of France.
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-100">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-100">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           Formerly singular of the now invariable
           <i>
            mille
           </i>
           ,
           <i>
            mil
           </i>
           is now only used in formal documents to write dates between
           <i>
            mil un
           </i>
           (1001) and
           <i>
            mil neuf cent quatre-vingt-dix-neuf
           </i>
           (1999).
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
            <a href="#cite_note-99">
             [94]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-thousandByHundreds-103">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           ^
           <a href="#cite_ref-thousandByHundreds_103-0">
            <sup>
             <i>
              <b>
               a
              </b>
             </i>
            </sup>
           </a>
           <a href="#cite_ref-thousandByHundreds_103-1">
            <sup>
             <i>
              <b>
               b
              </b>
             </i>
            </sup>
           </a>
           <a href="#cite_ref-thousandByHundreds_103-2">
            <sup>
             <i>
              <b>
               c
              </b>
             </i>
            </sup>
           </a>
           <a href="#cite_ref-thousandByHundreds_103-3">
            <sup>
             <i>
              <b>
               d
              </b>
             </i>
            </sup>
           </a>
           <a href="#cite_ref-thousandByHundreds_103-4">
            <sup>
             <i>
              <b>
               e
              </b>
             </i>
            </sup>
           </a>
           <a href="#cite_ref-thousandByHundreds_103-5">
            <sup>
             <i>
              <b>
               f
              </b>
             </i>
            </sup>
           </a>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           While both styles are correct and concurrently used, numbers above
           <i>
            mille
           </i>
           and under
           <i>
            deux mille
           </i>
           are usually counted by hundreds from
           <i>
            onze cents
           </i>
           up to
           <i>
            seize cent quatre-vingt-dix-neuf
           </i>
           and are then indifferently counted both styles
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
            <a href="#cite_note-101">
             [95]
            </a>
           </sup>
           in informal language while the count by adding hundreds to one thousand, like in
           <i>
            mille cent
           </i>
           ,
           <i>
            mille six cents
           </i>
           , is favoured in written language, especially in juridical, administrative and scientific works.
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
            <a href="#cite_note-102">
             [96]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-105">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-105">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <i>
            Nota Bene
           </i>
           that English use the short scale while French use the long scale.
          </span>
         </li>
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>

         <i>
          Pouvez-vous m’aider s’il vous plaît ?
         </i>
         /
         <i>
          Pourriez-vous m’aider s’il vous plaît ?
         </i>
         (formal) or
         <i>
          Peux-tu m’aider s’il te plaît ?
         </i>
         /
         <i>
          Pourrais-tu m’aider s’il te plaît
         </i>
         (informal)
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [puve vu mɛːde sɪl vu plɛ]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [puve vu mede sil vu plɛ]
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         Where are the toilets?
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          Où sont les toilettes ?
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [u sõ le twalɛt]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="nounderlines nowrap">
          <span class="unicode haudio">

             </a>
            </span>
            <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/29/Fr-O%C3%B9_sont_les_toilettes.oga" title="Fr-Où sont les toilettes.oga">

              [u sõ le twalɛt]

         Do you speak English?

        <td>
         <i>
          Parlez-vous (l')anglais ? / Est-ce que vous parlez (l')anglais ?
         </i>

        <td>
         <span class="nounderlines nowrap">
          <span class="unicode haudio">

             </a>
            </span>
            <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1c/Fr-Est-ce_que_vous_parlez_l%27anglais.oga" title="Fr-Est-ce que vous parlez l'anglais.oga">
             <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
              [ɛs kœ vu paʁle lãɡlɛ]

           </span>
          </span>
         </span>

        <td>
         <span class="nounderlines nowrap">
          <span class="unicode haudio">

             </a>

         <i>
          Je ne sais pas.
         </i>

         <i>
          Je ne sais.
         </i>

         <span class="nounderlines nowrap">

        </td>

          J’ai soif.

        <td>
         I am hungry.
        </td>

          J’ai faim.
         </i>
         (literally, "I have hunger")
        </td>

       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         How are you? / How are things going? / How is everything?
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          Comment allez-vous ?
         </i>
         (formal) or
         <i>
          Ça va ?
         </i>
         /
         <i>
          Comment ça va ?
         </i>
         (informal)
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [kɔmã t‿ale vu]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [kɔmɒ̃ t‿ale vu]
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         I am (very) well / Things are going (very) well // Everything is (very) well
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          Je vais (très) bien
         </i>
         (formal) or
         <i>
          Ça va (très) bien.
         </i>
         /
         <i>
          Tout va (très) bien
         </i>
         (informal)
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ʒœ vɛ (tʁɛ) bjẽ]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ʒø vɛ (tʁɛ) bjæ̃]
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         I am (very) bad / Things are (very) bad / Everything is (very) bad
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          Je vais (très) mal
         </i>
         (formal) or
         <i>
          Ça va (très) mal
         </i>
         /
         <i>
          Tout va (très) mal
         </i>
         (informal)
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ʒœ vɛ (tʁɛ) mal]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ʒø vɛ (tʁɛ) mal]
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         I am all right/so-so / Everything is all right/so-so
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          Assez bien
         </i>
         or
         <i>
          Ça va comme ci, comme ça
         </i>
         or simply
         <i>
          Ça va.
         </i>
         . (Sometimes said: « Couci, couça. », informal: "bof") i.e. « Comme ci, comme ça. »)
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ase bjẽ]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ase bjæ̃]
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         I am fine.
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          Ça va bien.
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [sa vɔ bjẽ]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [sa va bjæ̃]
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         (How) may I help you? / Do you need help? /
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          (Comment) puis-je vous aider ? Avez-vous besoin d'aide ?
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [(kɔmã) pɥiʒ vu z‿ɛːde]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [(kɔmɑ̃) pɥiʒ vu z‿ede]
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>

            </q>

         <li id="cite_note-Benet-MartínezHong2014-18">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-Benet-MartínezHong2014_18-0">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation">
            Novoa, Cristina; Moghaddam, Fathali M. (2014).
            <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=gAqKAwAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA468" rel="nofollow">
             "Applied Perspectives: Policies for Managing Cultural Diversity"
            </a>
            . In Benet-Martínez, Verónica; Hong, Ying-Yi.
            <i>
             The Oxford Handbook of Multicultural Identity
            </i>
            . Oxford Library of Psychology. New York: Oxford University Press. p. 468.
            <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
             ISBN
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-979669-4" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-19-979669-4">
             978-0-19-979669-4
            </a>
            .
            <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress_Control_Number" title="Library of Congress Control Number">
             LCCN
            </a>
            <a class="external text" href="//lccn.loc.gov/2014006430" rel="nofollow">
             2014006430
            </a>
            .
            <a href="/wiki/OCLC" title="OCLC">
             OCLC
            </a>
            <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/oclc/871965715" rel="nofollow">
             871965715
            </a>
            .
            <q>
             It is important to note, however, that not all countries have an official language. Until 1992, France had discouraged the use of regional languages ... in schools and businesses but had stopped short of making an official language declaration. In 1992, the government ratified ... a constitutional amendment that made French the sole official language of the Republic ...
            </q>
           </cite>

          </span>

            "En Afrique, il est impossible de parler d'une forme unique du français mais..."
           </a>

         <li id="cite_note-31">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-31">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.diplomatie.gouv.fr/en/France-priorities_1/francophony-french-language_1113/french-language_1934/french-language-in-the-world_3441/the-french-language-in-the-world-an-expanding-community_4289.html" rel="nofollow">
            France-Diplomatie
           </a>
           <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20090727195522/http://www.diplomatie.gouv.fr/en/France-priorities_1/francophony-french-language_1113/french-language_1934/french-language-in-the-world_3441/the-french-language-in-the-world-an-expanding-community_4289.html" rel="nofollow">
            Archived
           </a>
           27 July 2009 at the
           <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">
            Wayback Machine
           </a>
           . "Furthermore, the demographic growth of Southern hemisphere countries leads us to anticipate a new increase in the overall number of French speakers."
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-32">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-32">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <span class="languageicon">
            (in French)
           </span>
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.cecif.com/?page=la_francophonie" rel="nofollow">
            "Le français, langue en évolution. Dans beaucoup de pays francophones, surtout sur le continent africain, une proportion importante de la population ne parle pas couramment le français (même s'il est souvent la langue officielle du pays). Ce qui signifie qu'au fur et à mesure que les nouvelles générations vont à l'école, le nombre de francophones augmente : on estime qu'en 2015, ceux-ci seront deux fois plus nombreux qu'aujourd'hui.
           </a>
           "
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-33">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-33">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <span class="languageicon">
            (in French)
           </span>
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.cecif.com/?page=la_francophonie#francaisafrique" rel="nofollow">
            c) Le sabir franco-africain
           </a>
           :
           <i>
            <span lang="fr">
             "C'est la variété du français la plus fluctuante. Le sabir franco-africain est instable et hétérogène sous toutes ses formes. Il existe des énoncés où les mots sont français mais leur ordre reste celui de la langue africaine. En somme, autant les langues africaines sont envahies par les structures et les mots français, autant la langue française se métamorphose en Afrique, donnant naissance à plusieurs variétés."
            </span>
           </i>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-34">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-34">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <span class="languageicon">
            (in French)
           </span>
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.tlfq.ulaval.ca/axl/afrique/centrafrique.htm" rel="nofollow">
            République centrafricaine
           </a>
           :
           <i>
            <span lang="fr">
             Il existe une autre variété de français, beaucoup plus répandue et plus permissive : le français local. C'est un français très influencé par les langues centrafricaines, surtout par le sango. Cette variété est parlée par les classes non instruites, qui n'ont pu terminer leur scolarité. Ils utilisent ce qu'ils connaissent du français avec des emprunts massifs aux langues locales. Cette variété peut causer des problèmes de compréhension avec les francophones des autres pays, car les interférences linguistiques, d'ordre lexical et sémantique, sont très importantes.
            </span>
           </i>
           (
           <i>
            One example of a variety of African French that is difficult to understand for European French speakers
           </i>
           ).
          </span>
         </li>

             "Septante, octante (huitante), nonante"
            </a>
            .
            <i>
             langue-fr.net
            </i>
            (in French).
           </cite>
           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=langue-fr.net&amp;rft.atitle=Septante%2C+octante+%28huitante%29%2C+nonante&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.langue-fr.net%2Fspip.php%3Farticle202&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFrench+language">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
           </span>
           . See also the English Wikipedia article on
           <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">
            Welsh language
           </a>
           , especially the section "Counting system" and its note on the influence of

            Celtic
           </a>
           in the French counting system.

         <li id="cite_note-92">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-92">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation web">
            <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20150101052809/http://xn--acadmie-franaise-npb1a.fr/la-langue-francaise/questions-de-langue#57_strong-em-nombres-criture-lecture-accord-em-strong" rel="nofollow">
             "Questions de langue: Nombres (écriture, lecture, accord)"
            </a>
            (in French).
            <a href="/wiki/Acad%C3%A9mie_fran%C3%A7aise" title="Académie française">
             Académie française
            </a>
            . Archived from
            <a class="external text" href="http://académie-française.fr/la-langue-francaise/questions-de-langue#57_strong-em-nombres-criture-lecture-accord-em-strong" rel="nofollow">
             the original
            </a>
            on 1 January 2015
            <span class="reference-accessdate">
             . Retrieved
             <span class="nowrap">
              15 November
             </span>
             2015
            </span>
            .
            <q>
             <i>
              Dans un souci de lisibilité, on sépare les milliers par une espace insécable dans les nombres exprimant une quantité :
             </i>
             1 000 m
             <i>
              ,
             </i>
             342 234 euros
             <i>
              ,
             </i>
             1 234 °C
             <i>
              , etc.
              <br/>
              En revanche, dans les nombres ayant fonction de numérotage (pages, dates, articles de code), les chiffres ne sont jamais séparés :
             </i>
             page 1254 of the 1992 edition, article 1246 of the Civil Code.
             <i>
              <br/>
              La virgule (et non le point comme chez les anglo‑saxons) sépare la partie entière de la partie décimale :
             </i>
             π vaut environ 3,14
             <i>
              ;
             </i>
             14,5 est la moitié de 29
             <i>
              .
             </i>
            </q>
           </cite>
           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Questions+de+langue%3A+Nombres+%28%C3%A9criture%2C+lecture%2C+accord%29&amp;rft.pub=Acad%C3%A9mie+fran%C3%A7aise&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Facad%C3%A9mie-fran%C3%A7aise.fr%2Fla-langue-francaise%2Fquestions-de-langue%2357_strong-em-nombres-criture-lecture-accord-em-strong&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFrench+language">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
           </span>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-93">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-99">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-99">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation web">
            <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20150101052809/http://xn--acadmie-franaise-npb1a.fr/la-langue-francaise/questions-de-langue#11_strong-em-an-deux-mil-ou-an-deux-mille-em-strong" rel="nofollow">
             "Questions de langue: 'An deux mil' ou 'an deux mille'?"
            </a>
            (in French).
            <a href="/wiki/Acad%C3%A9mie_fran%C3%A7aise" title="Académie française">
             Académie française
            </a>
            . Archived from
            <a class="external text" href="http://académie-française.fr/la-langue-francaise/questions-de-langue#11_strong-em-an-deux-mil-ou-an-deux-mille-em-strong" rel="nofollow">
             the original
            </a>
            on 1 January 2015
            <span class="reference-accessdate">
             . Retrieved
             <span class="nowrap">
              15 November
             </span>
             2015
            </span>
            .
            <q>
             <i>
              L’Académie n’admet (et ne privilégie) la variante
             </i>
             mil
             <i>
              de
             </i>
             mille
             <i>
              , dans les dates, que lorsque le numéral au singulier est suivi d’un ou plusieurs autres nombres.
             </i>
            </q>
           </cite>
           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Questions+de+langue%3A+%E2%80%98An+deux+mil%E2%80%99+ou+%E2%80%98an+deux+mille%E2%80%99%3F&amp;rft.pub=Acad%C3%A9mie+fran%C3%A7aise&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Facad%C3%A9mie-fran%C3%A7aise.fr%2Fla-langue-francaise%2Fquestions-de-langue%2311_strong-em-an-deux-mil-ou-an-deux-mille-em-strong&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFrench+language">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
           </span>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-101">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-101">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation book">
            <i>
             Lexique des règles typographiques en usage à l'imprimerie nationale
            </i>
            (in French) (6th ed.). Paris:
            <a href="/wiki/Imprimerie_nationale" title="Imprimerie nationale">
             Imprimerie nationale
            </a>
            . March 2011. p. 41.
            <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
             ISBN
            </a>
            <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-2-7433-0482-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-2-7433-0482-9">
             978-2-7433-0482-9
            </a>
            .
           </cite>
           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Lexique+des+r%C3%A8gles+typographiques+en+usage+%C3%A0+l%27imprimerie+nationale&amp;rft.place=Paris&amp;rft.pages=41&amp;rft.edition=6th&amp;rft.pub=Imprimerie+nationale&amp;rft.date=2011-03&amp;rft.isbn=978-2-7433-0482-9&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFrench+language">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
           </span>
           <i>
            Au-delà de mille, on compte habituellement : ↲ onze, douze, treize, quatorze, quinze, seize cents ↲ plutôt que : ↲ mille cent, mille deux cents, mille trois cents... ↲ mais on emploiera indifféremment : ↲ dix-sept cents ou mille sept cents...
           </i>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-102">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-102">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation web">
            <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20150101052809/http://xn--acadmie-franaise-npb1a.fr/la-langue-francaise/questions-de-langue#57_strong-em-nombres-criture-lecture-accord-em-strong" rel="nofollow">
             "Questions de langue: Nombres (écriture, lecture, accord)"
            </a>
            (in French).
            <a href="/wiki/Acad%C3%A9mie_fran%C3%A7aise" title="Académie française">
             Académie française
            </a>
            . Archived from
            <a class="external text" href="http://académie-française.fr/la-langue-francaise/questions-de-langue#57_strong-em-nombres-criture-lecture-accord-em-strong" rel="nofollow">
             the original
            </a>
            on 1 January 2015
            <span class="reference-accessdate">
             . Retrieved
             <span class="nowrap">
              15 November
             </span>
             2015
            </span>
            .
            <q>
             <i>
              Pour les dates (et les nombres en général) entre 1000 et 2000, il y a concurrence entre deux lectures :
             </i>
             mille six cent trente‑cinq
             <i>
              ou
             </i>
             seize cent trente‑cinq
             <i>
              .
              <br/>
              Aucune de ces formes ne peut être considérée comme fautive. Cependant, dans l’usage courant, on dit plutôt
             </i>
             onze cents
             <i>
              ,
             </i>
             douze cents
             <i>
              , etc. :
             </i>
             onze cents francs
             <i>
              ,
             </i>
             seize cents euros
             <i>
              , tandis que dans la langue écrite, et notamment dans un texte juridique, administratif ou scientifique, on préférera les formes :
             </i>
             mille cent
             <i>
              ,
             </i>
             mille deux cents
             <i>
              , etc.
             </i>
            </q>
           </cite>
           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Questions+de+langue%3A+Nombres+%28%C3%A9criture%2C+lecture%2C+accord%29&amp;rft.pub=Acad%C3%A9mie+fran%C3%A7aise&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Facad%C3%A9mie-fran%C3%A7aise.fr%2Fla-langue-francaise%2Fquestions-de-langue%2357_strong-em-nombres-criture-lecture-accord-em-strong&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFrench+language">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
           </span>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-104">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-104">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation web">
            <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20150101052809/http://xn--acadmie-franaise-npb1a.fr/la-langue-francaise/questions-de-langue#57_strong-em-nombres-criture-lecture-accord-em-strong" rel="nofollow">
             "Questions de langue: Nombres (écriture, lecture, accord)"
            </a>
            (in French).
            <a href="/wiki/Acad%C3%A9mie_fran%C3%A7aise" title="Académie française">
             Académie française
            </a>
            . Archived from
            <a class="external text" href="http://académie-française.fr/la-langue-francaise/questions-de-langue#57_strong-em-nombres-criture-lecture-accord-em-strong" rel="nofollow">
             the original
            </a>
            on 1 January 2015
            <span class="reference-accessdate">
             . Retrieved
             <span class="nowrap">
              15 November
             </span>
             2015
            </span>
            .
            <q>
             Vingt et cent se terminent par un
             <i>
              s
             </i>
             quand ils sont précédés d’un nombre qui les multiplie, mais ils restent invariables s’ils sont suivis d’un autre nombre ou de
             <i>
              mille
             </i>
             . On dira ainsi :
             <i>
              deux cents euros
             </i>
             mais
             <i>
              deux cent vingt euros
             </i>
             ;
             <i>
              quatre‑vingts hommes
             </i>
             mais
             <i>
              quatre‑vingt‑deux hommes
             </i>
             . Ils restent également invariables lorsqu’ils sont employés comme adjectifs numéraux ordinaux :
             <i>
              page deux cent
             </i>
             ;
             <i>
              page quatre‑vingt
             </i>
             ;
             <i>
              l’an mille neuf cent
             </i>
             .
             <br/>
             En revanche,
             <i>
              vingt
             </i>
             et
             <i>
              cent
             </i>
             varient devant
             <i>
              millier
             </i>
             ,
             <i>
              million
             </i>
             ,
             <i>
              milliard
             </i>
             , qui sont des noms et non des adjectifs numéraux :
             <i>
              deux cents millions d’années
             </i>
             ;
             <i>
              trois cents milliers d’habitants
             </i>
             .
            </q>
            <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Questions+de+langue%3A+Nombres+%28%C3%A9criture%2C+lecture%2C+accord%29&amp;rft.pub=Acad%C3%A9mie+fran%C3%A7aise&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Facad%C3%A9mie-fran%C3%A7aise.fr%2Fla-langue-francaise%2Fquestions-de-langue%2357_strong-em-nombres-criture-lecture-accord-em-strong&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFrench+language">
             <span style="display:none;">
             </span>
            </span>
           </cite>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-106">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-106">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation web">
            <a class="external text" href="http://www.academie-francaise.fr/ne" rel="nofollow">
             "Ne"
            </a>
            .
            <i>
             Dire, Ne pas dire
            </i>
            . Académie française. 3 November 2011
            <span class="reference-accessdate">
             . Retrieved
             <span class="nowrap">
              30 May
             </span>
             2014
            </span>
            .
           </cite>
           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Dire%2C+Ne+pas+dire&amp;rft.atitle=Ne&amp;rft.date=2011-11-03&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.academie-francaise.fr%2Fne&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFrench+language">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
           </span>
           <i>
            On néglige trop souvent de faire entendre l’adverbe ne, en faisant de pas l’unique marque de négation : Je veux pas, je sais pas. Cette habitude, répandue dans le langage parlé, est une véritable faute.
           </i>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-107">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-107">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation web">
            <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnrtl.fr/definition/pas" rel="nofollow">
             "Pas"
            </a>
            .
            <i>
             Trésor de la langue française informatisé
            </i>
            . Analyse et traitement informatique de la langue française
            <span class="reference-accessdate">
             . Retrieved
             <span class="nowrap">
              30 May
             </span>
             2014
            </span>
            .
           </cite>
           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Tr%C3%A9sor+de+la+langue+fran%C3%A7aise+informatis%C3%A9&amp;rft.atitle=Pas&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.cnrtl.fr%2Fdefinition%2Fpas&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFrench+language">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
           </span>
           <i>
            − Pop. ou très fam. [Avec suppression de ne]
           </i>
          </span>
         </li>
        </ol>
       </div>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Organizations">
        Organizations
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.fondation-alliancefr.org/" rel="nofollow">
         Fondation Alliance française
        </a>
        : an international organization for the promotion of French language and culture
        <span class="languageicon">
         (in French)
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.fle.fr/en/" rel="nofollow">
         Agence de promotion du FLE
        </a>
        : Agency for promoting French as a foreign language
       </li>
      </ul>

               <div>
                <div class="hlist hlist-separated">
                 <ul>
                  <li>
                   <i>
                    Italics
                   </i>
                   indicate
                   <a href="/wiki/Language_death" title="Language death">
                    extinct languages
                   </a>
                  </li>
                  <li>
                   <b>
                    Bold
                   </b>
                   indicates
                   <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_number_of_native_speakers" title="List of languages by number of native speakers">
                    languages with more than 5 million speakers
                   </a>
                  </li>
                  <li>
                   Languages between parentheses are
                   <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)" title="Variety (linguistics)">
                    varieties
                   </a>
                   of the language on their left.
                  </li>
                 </ul>
